I made this recipe and it was yummy.  However, I suggest that you only fill the muffin cups 2/3 of the way, instead of 3/4 because they end up looking like muffins (way too high), rather than cupcakes.  I will also probably lessen the milk a bit the next time, because it came out too soft and was disintegrating people were eating it.

text:
These cupcakes are pretty good, but nothing exceptional.  Also, the instructions are misleading; they say to cream 3 Tbsp. of butter with 1 1/2 cups of sugar. It's virtually impossible to cream such a small amount of butter with 8 times the amount of sugar!  The butter will never get creamy, but will stay overly grainy and sugary from all that sugar.  A much better and simpler way is to melt the butter and add it to the wet ingredients, and then add the sugar to the dry ingredients. The best part about these cupcakes is they are lowfat!

text:
Very easy and tasty (with and without icing).  I found that it will make 30 cupcakes (don't fill each cup as full as stated, closer to 1/2).  They will be the perfect size for icing.  If you aren't planning on icing them you could make 24 cupcakes.  I made these with the help of a 3 yr old and a 1 yr old.  They both love them!  I did need to bake them a bit longer (about 10 min) but our oven usually needs a bit longer so others might not not need to.

text:
This recipe is great! My cupcakes came out light and airy. The batter was the consistency of thick mousse.
I made 3 changes:
1 - I used almost double the butter. It made creaming the sugar much easier and added a creamy flavor.
2 - I used a full TBSP of vanilla

I will also say that the yield is much higher than stated - I filled my cups 1/2 way and got almost double the amount of cupcakes. They rose beautifully.

If cooking in silicone pans, add about 3 minutes to your cooking time.

text:
Very unsatisfactory recipe.  It says it makes 30 cupcakes, but really it only makes 16.  If you fill the cups 3/4 full as the recipe indicates, the cupcakes dome too high.  The muffin cups should only be filled a scant 2/3 full for the proper height.  The flavor is only so-so and the texture is dry and too dense.  They were extremely easy to make, which is why I chose the recipe.  But I would not make them again. I made these for my son's second grade class...if I were making them for adults with more discriminating palates, I would toss them and start over with a different recipe.

text:
OK That's it! This is the best recipe for chocolate cupcakes from now on. I used margarine instead of butter and replaced the vanilla essence with chocolate essence for extra choc flavour and they turned out beautifully. My new silicone cases worked a treat with a fine mist of canola oil before filling, no sticking and no need to run around picking up paper wrappers in the aftermath. No frosting required. Perhaps a little dusting of icing sugar if you can't resist making them prettier. The recipe made 26 nicely sized cupcakes for all the little kids at playgroup.

text:
Yum Yum! There's just something about a good chocolate cupcake and a cold glass of milk! This is a good chocolate cupcake. I read through ALL the reviews and decided to try the recipe "as is". I was happy that i did because it came out perfectly...chocolatey tasting and moist. The only thing I did do that others had suggested was to fill them 2/3 of the way full instead of 3/4. Doing this resulted in the cupcake rising just over the edge of the cupcake papers...perfect! I used unsweetened cocoa powder from King Arthur Flour, so it was a good quality cocoa powder and the flavor of the cupcake was all chocolate! Thank you!

text:
Suggestions;
First, sift together all the dry ingredients *including the sugar*. Melt the butter. It's cool, these aren't cookies. Add the milk to the dry ingredients first. Add the eggs one at a time. Add the melted butter. Add vanilla. Fill these between 1/3 and 1/2 full. They came out perfect. Filling to that level, I got 22, which is great because I need to make 33 and I know now that I can halve the recipe for the next batch and get exactly the right amount. By turning the temp dial to between 375 and 400, I was able to cook these in 22 minutes.

text:
This is a very rich, true chocolate cupcake. If you want a milk chocolate cupcake or a lighter chocolate taste, this is not the cupcake for you. If you're like me and love chocolate, this is a fantastic moist cupcake.

Tips:
When the recipe says "cream together the butter and sugar" they don't mean cream. They mean mix really well. The butter is not going to cream because the ratio of butter to sugar is too low. It's going to look like more of a wet sand (clumpy sugar) than your normal cream. That's fine. The end result is delicious, and the cupcake gets the extra moisture when you add the eggs in the next step.

I also filled the cups closer to 2/3rds full, and it worked out perfectly. I paired it with a fantastic rich buttercream frosting.

I followed the recipe exactly.  If you make 18 cupcakes they will overflow the liners considerably, which isn't bad if your children like the frosted tops more than the cake bottom!  It does present a problem getting them out of the tins, however.  If I make these again I would spray the tin after I put in the liners OR make smaller cupcakes. I was a little disappointed when I took them out of the oven, but they looked okay once frosted ( use extra heavy amount of frosting to make them look mounded on top), and they tasted very good.  I don't make cupcakes often, but it was a request from a grandchild, so I did.  I will keep this recipe on file because they WERE tasty, but if I make them again I will know better what to expect. I had extra French buttercream frosting left over from filling macarons, so I thought I'd make some cupcakes to use it up. But the result is a spongy cupcake that tastes like it's a low-fat, gluten-free abomination. Sure it can be fixed with buttercream frosting, but almost anything can, n'est-ce pas?

All the proportions are suspect: most egregious is the doubling-up of baking powder, which adds to the bitterness, since baking powder contains acid. That might be OK if alkali Dutch-process chocolate was specified, but it isn't.

This recipe is simply not up to the level I've come to expect from this site.

text:
I made this recipe exactly according to the instructions, and found the batter too runny; the recipe almost certainly needs more flour and less in each cupcake.

As the recipe stands, it's delicious if put in the microwave in a mug for about 2 minutes on high. In the oven, though, it spills outwards and takes longer to cook than it calls for. Honestly, I think this recipe may have been devised at a high altitude, so at nearly sea level, this didn't work correctly at all.

Tl;dr: the flavor of this recipe is amazing, but the consistency is horrible. I suggest adjusting flour and milk levels accordingly.

text:
I followed the recipe exactly, right down to every sift, cream, stir, and beat. The cupcakes were dry and stuck to the wrappers like cement. They also completely overflowed and turned into giant brick-like muffins instead of moist dainty cupcakes.

I tried them again today, only I doubled the butter and added a quarter cup more milk, and I only filled the cups 1/3 or 1/4 of the way. This time they turned out perfect, so the only flaw in the recipe is the butter. I think the author made a mistake recording the butter, because 3 TBs simply isn't enough to provide proper moisture to not only prevent the cupcakes from sticking to the wrapper, but to keep the cupcakes moist.

This is a great basic chocolate cupcake recipe.  I agree with other posters, however, that the directions and serving size is a little off.  As another suggested, I melted the butter and added with the wet ingredients.  Using a hand mixer, I beat everything for two minutes (like the directions for a boxed cake).  I was able to get 24 perfect sized cupcakes from this recipe, instead of 16 as is stated.  But the overall taste is good and this will probably be my go-to chocolate cupcake recipe.  Thanks for sharing!

I agree with the other reviewers that the recipe makes way too much - I halved it and made exactly 12 cupcakes (batter filled halfway).  Some other changes - 1) instead of creaming the butter with the sugar, I melted it, and added it to the eggs when cool.  2) couldn't find my baking soda, so I left it out.  3) added walnuts to the bottom of the baking cup before filling with batter.

I used this recipe on a whim... it was just an after dinner "I feel like making cupcakes" thing and I thought I would change it up a bit, rather than using my tried-and-true. The only change I made was to add some Hershey's chocolate syrup (from the can) to make things a bit more rich and moist. The resulting cupcakes were yet dry and rather bitter. I topped them with extremely rich buttercream frosting to even out the tastes, but the cakes themselves still crumbled from lack of moisture. Everything I bake is always raved about... I'm glad this was just an experiment for private consumption!

text:
The first time I tried this recipe, it turned out better than my original chocolate cupcake. But I still wasn't satisfied with its texture. It needed to be more moist. So I substituted milk with heavy cream, and the all-purpose flour with cake flour, and it was amazing! Everyone loved it. A friend of mine whom I have given these cupcakes as a gift described it as [a bite of] "heaven"! 

Just a little caution, since I used cake flour instead of all-purpose flour, it won't give you a beautiful dome shape. But, according to my taste buds, it will give you a softer cupcake. Also, I baked them for 25 minutes because 15 minutes will give me cupcakes that falls apart when I eat them. 25 minutes gives me cupcakes with a bit crunchy outside, and a moist inside. :)

text:
I have made these cupcakes on two occasions (one week apart to note the weather/humidity hadn't changed) and I found it to be very frustrating.  

The first time I cut the recipe in half and they came out almost perfect.  The flavor was spot, but even my fast cooking oven took the full 17 minutes and the cupcakes were oohey gooey...too oohey gooey.  Also, cutting the recipe in half should have made 8 cupcakes, but it made 10 with a little batter left over.

The second time I tried to make these I followed the directions exactly as shown and these were a nightmare!  It made 20 cupcakes, 6 of them caved in on themselves, 4 of them rose over the liners, 6 of them cracked and I had 4 pretty good ones.  I baked them for 18 minutes, rotating the pan half way through and all of them came out too gooey, even the cracked ones.  Thankfully icing was able to cover that, but sunken cupcakes?  That's embarrassing.  

I'm willing to accept that some of this can come from over beating, but I think the measurements are a little off.  I might try it again, but play around with the measurements because the flavor was there.  It just needs some tweaking.

text:
I followed the recipe and just substituted buttermilk for the milk, and added 2 teaspoons of brewed coffee.  And just made it an even 1 teaspoon of vanilla.  Mine needed to bake 18-20 minutes.

The 3 Tbl softened butter and sugar do get a moist and fluffy sandy texture instead of creamy.  But, once you add the eggs it is fine.  I got 18 cupcakes out of this batter and it was like a mousse/pudding consistancy and yummy.  I do like that this is a low fat treat and I didn't need to load up on butter or oil.  I made a vanilla cream cheese frosting and they taste very good.  The do taste good without icing.  They were moist and fluffy.  Will be making again!

Made this for my mother-in-law's birthday and ended up with enough batter for 30. I measured a full ice cream scoop per cupcake and they came out PERFECTLY! I added a tablespoon of Kahlua to the measuring cup, and then continued to fill the cup with milk. The Kahlua gave the chocolate a little depth, and they were moist and wonderful! A cream cheese frosting (from The Joy of Cooking cookbook) on top made it even better! I will definitely make this recipe again.

text:
We've made this a couple times.  The first time we made the cupcakes using the exact recipe.  They turned out splendidly.  We used silicone baking cups and a small glass cake pan to make cupcakes & a small cake.  The cupcake had a bit of difficulty coming out of the baking cup, but we believe that was because we didn't let them cool long enough before removing them.    The second time we cut the sugar to 1 cup and changed it to 3/4 cup white and 1/4 cup brown sugar.  We used 1/4 cup tofu in place of one egg.  We added a bit more cocoa because there was cocoa in our tofu (we tried to make tofu pudding and couldn't get small enough chunks, so we used it in this recipe!)  The next time we make this, we are going to try to replace both eggs with tofu and maybe cut the sugar a bit more (3/4 cup?).    Overall this is a delightful recipe.  It doesn't need frosting-it is very sweet by itself.

Awesome recipe! I improvised based on what I had on hand. I traded the cocoa powder for a mix of unsweetened and regular melted chocolate and adjusted the sugar to 3/4 cup to accommodate. Used margarine instead of butter and only 3/4 cup of milk based on another review. These turned out fabulous and I had a difficult time keeping my fingers out of the batter! Made 12 overflowing cupcakes (I only had a 12 muffin tin)and topped them off with a chocolate mousse frosting; although they would have been just fine on their own.

These were awesome!  Very moist, I'm not sure how anyone had something bad to say about them. I had to cook them a little longer than the recipe suggested but other than that the recipe worked out for me, the serving size was accurate.

text:
I've been looking for a yummy chocolate cupcake and this is it! The ones I've tried all turned out too spongy, but this one is just right.
I did everything the same except I used Half&Half instead of milk, and instead of 1/4 tsp soda and 2 tsp powder, I did 3/4 tsp soda and 1 1/2 tsp powder to make it chewier. I don't know much about baking, so I'm not sure if it changed how it would have turned out, but they were just how I wanted them!
I don't like things to be very sweet, and this wasn't. They balanced with the very sweet chocolate butter cream frosting I used.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
Great recipe... and of course I made a few changes. (We usually do.) Since I have a wheat allergy, I made the following changes:
1) I used "Pamela's Gluten-Free +Vegan Artisan Blend +Whole Grain 1 to 1 Wheat Flour Replacement Flour" (That's a mouthful but worth it.) Likewise, I used gluten-free baking powder.
2) I also upped the butter to 5T and added a whole banana for moisture to cream with the sugar (which I put only a cup and maybe a pinch.. the amount of sugar that this called for was insane.) We like the banana and chocolate combo- otherwise, I would have gone with 6T of butter for sure.
3) I also added chocolate chips and a good old squirt of Hershey's syrup for luck.
I was able to get 22 out of the mixture. They baked to perfection in about 16 minutes @ 350 /convection. Once cooled they were topped off with a dark chocolate drizzle. When cooking recipes, you have to be creative and adjust for your own needs.

This was a really easy and simple recipe and the out come was great but if you are  perfectionist like me or want a more traditional cupcake look (more dome-like top) then i suggest you fill the liners up 1/2 way or 2/3 the way up and bake them at 325F for a bit longer. I made one batch at the recommended 3/4 the way up at 350 and instead of rising they flattened out and spread like cookies and the outside seemed to be cooking a lot faster than the insides. I fixed the amount in the liner and the temperature and they looked a lot better.

I made these exactly as the recipe suggested. I was a bit concerned with the little bit of fat and these possibly being dry, but they aren't. They are pleasantly moist and light. My biggest issue is that they just don't really taste chocolatey enough.  I would be interested to add some mini chocolate chips next time to get that gooy chocolate flavoure when you bite into them.
I used a Pampered Chefs large scoop which measures 3Tbsp for each cup. I also used one Pampered Chef stone muffin pan and a metal muffin tin pan. I found that the ones in the metal pan rose quite considerabley than the ones in the stone pan, they seemed too cook slower and did not rise past the pan edge. 
No muffins stuck to my pans, but I oiled them all very well.

text:
Wonderful recipe!  It will be my chocolate cupcake recipe from here on out.  Here are some notes from what I did.

I. One person said to add less milk.  While I would agree if you plan on making and baking all of them in one setting.  I did that at first and agree they were a bit too soft for what I like.  I would say that the milk amount is perfect if you plan on refrigerating them and making them when the batter is cold.

II.  Sift the flour and cocoa powder!  I didn't.  While they were still great, I think they could have been fluffier and the batter smoother if I wasn't too lazy to do so.

III.  I think you can add  to them because the recipe allows is.  I added 3/4 a cup of dark chocolate chips (used up the bag) and it added so much more chocolate flavor.  I think adding nuts or fruit would add so much more depth to this than  just your standard cupcake.

IV.  I didn't add any frosting.  My wife and I hate the stuff.

text:
While making these for the first time I cursed this recipe. 3 tbsp of butter is an odd measurement for butter. Also, 1/8 tsp is an odd measurement as well. So there was a bit of guesstimation. In the future, to make things easier, I will just use 1/4 cup of butter. And another reviewer was correct in that you cannot cream the butter and sugar. You're basically just evenly distributing the butter through the sugar. Also, next time I will try 1 cup sugar and 1/2 cup honey to cut down on sweetness. 
Now, that brings me to flavor. O. M. G. So flippin yummy!!! Tastes more like a brownie than chocolate cake. I added some cinnamon and the batter tasted like hot cocoa.
Like other people have said, only fill the cups half way. 3/4 is way too much for a reg size cupcake pan. Unless you're into that. I am. But it made it so I had to add 5 min to the cook time. I regret nothing, and have no desire to share these with anyone.
I made a pretty simple, not too sweet, lightly spiced butter cream to go with them.
I about died when I ate one.

Sigh, disappointing. I don't like to leave bad reviews, but I have to be brutally honest here. 
First off I had to add way more butter than was called for.  You cannot cream sugar and butter with that little bit of butter. Second, I improved (or at least I thought I did) upon the recipe by adding a whole melted Hershey bar as well as a splash of coffee to bring out the chocolate taste, but the cakes had hardly any chocolate flavor whatsoever. About the same as anything you get out of a box.  I have never experienced that before with other recipes. Generally, adding any actual chocolate and coffee make the taste way better. Also, I filled the baking cups 3/4 way as instructed and they overflowed and pretty much turned into hollow muffins. Several of them even fell apart and I had to put them into the garbage disposer. :(  Luckily, I made a yummy coffee icing from another recipe on hand that sort of saved the ones that were intact. If you are a super chocolate lover, I would avoid this recipe.

text:
These were delicious. I made them gluten free by substituting the wheat flour for rice flour plus 3/4 tsp xanthan gum. Works perfectly. One important note though -- the baking time is given as 15 minutes at 350, or until a toothpick inserted comes out clean. You're going to be inserting that toothpick continuously for the next 10 minutes. So just set the timer at 25 minutes and save yourself the trouble. The original recipe poster must have had an oven that ran really hot. My oven is true to temperature and I baked mine for 25 minutes exactly. Typically cupcakes take a lot longer than 15 minutes.

text:
This is so flavorful and so chocolaty! I made the following changes:
1: I add 1/4 cup 72% dark chocolate chips. 
2: I use 2 espresso shots (60 ml) with 180 ml fat-free milk to make the flavor stronger.
3. I reduce sugar to 1 1/4 cup 
The result is very intense chocolately cupcakes..... maybe a little too flavorful, I may omit chocolate  chips next time and try to use applesauce to reduce calories from fat., but the original recipe is good enough as it is.

text:
I made this recipe last night & the only thing I changed was the amount of butter. Instead of 3 TBSPS, I use about 6. The sugar does not blend well with only 3 TBSPNS. I did not like these cupcakes. I felt it was too heavy on the cocoa side, leaving my cupcakes a lil bitter. Also, if u fill the cups 2/3 full, u will get muffins. The only cupcake that came out looking like a cupcake was the cup I filled closer to a 1/4 full. Maybe too much baking powder in the recipe. Also, the cake is very crumbly & baking for 17 minutes dried out the cake. Or maybe the lack of oil. Overall, it's a nice basic recipe that needs some tweaking to make the kind of chocolate cupcake I am craving.

text:
I did not care for this recipe. I have made a number of recipes from this site and have made things from scratch before. In my years, I have undercooked things, ovecooked things, burned things, but nothing prepared me for this. I guess most others that tried this recipe had great success with it. When I saw the rating and that it had over 800 reviews, I figured it would be wonderful to try. I made the recipe as the directions stated, with the ingredients listed. I didn't change anything. The baking time seemed to vary a little between reviewers, so I just went with the time listed on the recipe. The amount of batter to put into the cups also varied with reviewers. I ended up filling the cups about halfway. Once in the oven, the cupcakes did okay at first. When I checked on them again, they had expanded up and over the cup edges and the batter was spreading across the cupcake pan as they all started to connect into a giant mess. The middles of them still looked a bit raw from my view through the oven window, so I continued to let them bake. By the time they were done, the batter had risen, overflowed and the middles had sunk down into the cups.

text:
I've made this twice now. The first time, I made it exactly as the directions and the batter was fluffy. The second time, I mixed all dry together then added the butter/liquid mixture. Not as fluffy but still worked out well.

The first time I made it, I went with the 15 min baking time, didn't seem like it was enough and let it go for another 5-7 minutes. When I took the first two trays (12 cupcakes) out of the oven, they sunk, HARD. Didn't really cook. The second two trays (10 cupcakes total), I baked for 30 minutes and they turned out well.

The second time, I just baked everything for 30 minutes and had no issues.

I also modified the recipe slightly each time. I added some raspberry sauce, I found in a cheesecake recipe, injected into the middle, and topped them off with cream cheese icing. I like how they turned out this way.

I'll keep this recipe and make it again.

Just tried out this recipe and exactly like what most commented...fill the cups half full, use 1/2 cup of butter and I melted it in the microwave and then poured it into the sugar which I reduced to 1 cup. That way I didn't have to use the mixer. I split the batch in half and added chocolate chips to the mix. My niece tried it and she preferred the one with the chocolate chips! All in all an easy recipe that makes lovely cupcakes!

text:
These were some pretty good cupcakes! So after going through a lot of the reviews and deciding to make them, I also took the advice of some others and used 1/2 stick of butter instead of 3 tbsp. While I was beating the butter and sugar it was crumbly which I kinda freaked out about, but it was ok so don't worry. Also, minor adjustment but I filled each cup about halfway full and they were the perfect height, not spilling over like a muffin. They were a tiny bit dry, but it was probably my fault for not watching them close enough while they were baking. I made some vanilla frosting and sprinkled some crushed candy cane on top and they were the perfect Christmas treats! :)
My only advice is watch them super closely becasue they will probably be done in less than 15 minutes.

I did not like these at all, however my kids loved them. They came out more like brownies than cake. They were very dense and thick. I do believe the only reason they came out moist was because instead of using milk I used buttermilk and added some sour cream to the mix. So I will give them 2 stars only because my kids loved them so I happy that it was not a total lost cause. The ONLY way I will make these again is if my kids ask me.

text:
This recipe isn't too bad. I used 3/4 cup of milk instead of the full cup, which may have been the reason that they didn't turn out quite as moist as I would have liked them to be. Also the chocolate was a bit too bitter for my liking, but they are still enjoyable none the less. I used an ice cream scoop to scoop the batter into the tins (it filled half way perfectly in everyone), which turned out to be the perfect amount for me, since the cupcakes rose a bit over the top. I think this is good recipe and would recommend it to others.

I had quite the adventure trying to make these. First I didn't have enough cocoa powder so i had to wait until my mom went shopping to get some more. Once I had the cocoa I mixed it all together and put it in the muffin cups it wasn't until I was done that I realized I forgot to put the eggs in, so back into the bowl everything went. Once the eggs were in and the mix was in the muffin cups again I realized that the pilot light in the oven was out, so my mom lights it and I try to preheat the oven. After 15 minuits the oven still wasn't warm and after some playing around with it we realize that the only way for the oven to heat up at all is to turn it on all the way so we baked the cupcakes by alternating the oven on at full blast and off. eventually they cooked and although they wern't quite right they wern't bad next time i hope that they'll work out properly.
